Chloe Moreau et al (2018), Current Biology https://doi.org/10.1016/j.cub.2018.11.009\n\nLimb position along the body is highly consistent within one species but very variable among vertebrates. Despite major advances in our understanding of limb patterning in three dimensions, how limbs reproducibly form along the antero-posterior axis remains largely unknown. Hox genes have long been suspected to control limb position; however, supporting evidences are mostly correlative and their role in this process is unclear.\n\nHere, we show that limb position is determined early in development through the action of Hox genes. Dynamic lineage analysis revealed that, during gastrulation, the forelimb, interlimb, and hindlimb fields are progressively generated and concomitantly patterned by the collinear activation of Hox genes in a two-step process.\n\nFirst, the sequential activation of Hoxb genes controls the relative position of their own collinear domains of expression in the forming lateral plate mesoderm, as demonstrated by functional perturbations during gastrulation. Then, within these collinear domains, we show that Hoxb4 anteriorly and Hox9 genes posteriorly, respectively, activate and repress the expression of the forelimb initiation gene Tbx5 and instruct the definitive position of the forelimb.\n\nFurthermore, by comparing the dynamics of Hoxb genes activation during zebra finch, chicken, and ostrich gastrulation, we provide evidences that changes in the timing of collinear Hox gene activation might underlie natural variation in forelimb position between different birds. Altogether, our results that characterize the cellular and molecular mechanisms underlying the regulation and natural variation of forelimb positioning in avians show a direct and early role for Hox genes in this process.\n\nGood channel: https://www.youtube.com/Dlium\nSubscribe, like and comment.\n\nGood website: https://www.dlium.com\nBookmark, subscribe and comment.", "title": "Timed Collinear Activation of Hox Genes during Gastrulation Controls the Avian Forelimb Position"}, "statistics": {"commentCount": "0", "viewCount": "76", "likeCount": "2", "dislikeCount": "0", "favoriteCount": "0"}, "contentDetails": {"duration": "PT1M26S"}}], "idx_paper": "10.1016/j.cub.2018.11.009"}, {"q": "10.1016/j.tree.2018.10.007", "items": [{"id": "Fi8u3AExPlQ", "snippet": {"publishedAt": "2018-11-19T12:34:52Z", "description": "Automatic quantification of migratory activity in a diurnal passerine migrant, the dunnock, Prunella modularis.\n\nBird\u2019s behaviour is tracked using a computer vision algorithm based on dynamic background subtraction\n\nIlieva, Bianco and \u00c5kesson (2018) - Humans Understand and Evaluate Its Behavior\nSonja Stange, Stefan Kopp\n\nHRI'20: ACM/IEEE International Conference on Human-Robot Interaction\nSession: Perceiving Robots\n\nAbstract\nSocial robots interacting with users in real-life environments will often show surprising or even undesirable behavior. In this paper we investigate whether a robot's ability to self-explain its behavior affects the users' perception and assessment of this behavior. We propose an explanation model based on humans' folk-psychological concepts and test different explanation strategies in specifically designed HRI scenarios with robot behaviors perceived as intentional, but differently surprising or desirable. All types of explanation strategies increased the understandability and desirability of the behaviors. Retrieved\u00a0January 29,\u00a02016.\n\n\nDistinguishing featuresEdit\n\nPlastic cups come in a variety of colours, textures and sizes.\n\nUsesPlastic cups are often used for gatherings where it would be inconvenient to wash dishes afterward, due to factors such as location or number of guests. Plastic cups can be used for storing most liquids, but hot liquids may melt or warp the material.\n\nEnvironmental issuesEdit\n\nFurther information:\u00a0Great Pacific garbage patch,\u00a0plastic waste, and\u00a0marine debris\n\nMost plastic cups are designed for\u00a0single uses\u00a0and then\u00a0disposal\u00a0or recycling.[1]\u00a0A\u00a0life cycle inventory\u00a0of a comparison of paper and plastic shows environmental effects of both with no clear winner.[2]\n\nProduction of 1 tonne (0.98 long tons; 1.1 short tons) of plastic cup emits 135 pounds (61\u00a0kg) of\u00a0green house gases.\n\nThe choice between\u00a0paper cups\u00a0and plastic cups has to do with the life of the item after use. A paper cup may\u00a0biodegrade\u00a0faster than a\u00a0Styrofoam cup\u00a0or a plastic cup. In general cardboard or paper takes one to three months for biodegradation, as the majority of the content, up to 95%, is made with wood chips. A plastic cup can take up to 90 years to biodegrade, depending on the type of plastic.\n\nPlastic cups are made with\u00a0oil, which is not a renewable source. On the other hand, paper cups can be sourced from forests which fall under\u00a0sustainable management.\n\nPlastic cups, especially those made with\u00a0polystyrene, are also a possible\u00a0health hazardas chemicals may leach into the beverage. This is more likely to happen with warm drinks (hot chocolate, tea and coffee) than with cold drinks.[\n\nReferencesEdit\n\n^\u00a0Schnurr, Riley E.J.; Alboiu, Vanessa; Chaudhary, Meenakshi; Corbett, Roan A.; Quanz, Meaghan E.; Sankar, Karthikeshwar; Srain, Harveer S.; Thavarajah, Venukasan; Xanthos, Dirk; Walker, Tony R. This benchmark was extended later to large temperature differences at moderate Rayleigh numbers where a steady solution is obtained [2-4]. While the Boussinesq solution is symmetric, the solution at large temperature differences is not, due to expansion and contraction of the fluid.\n\nIn our publication [5] we investigated larger Rayleigh numbers in 2D and found a second unsymmetry. The flow becomes turbulent on the hot wall, but not on the cold wall.\n\nThis video features a 3D extension of that investigation. The Rayleigh number is 5e9 and the non-dimensional temperature difference is (Th-Tc)/dT = 1.2. The cavity has an aspect ratio of height over width of 2. The flow field is visualized as iso-controud of the Q-criterion.\n\nWe see that the turbulence on the hot wall is much more pronounced than on the cold wall. Further, most of the hot wall is turbulent, while on the cold wall the turbulence just appears in the lower regions.\n\nThe code used in this simulation is VirtualFluidsGKS: https://www.tu-braunschweig.de/irmb/forschung/virtualfluids\n\nThis work was finanzed by the German Research Foundation (DFG) under the framework of Research Training Group GRK 2075, https://www.tu-braunschweig.de/grk-2075.\n\n The video was generated on a desktop computer provided by Azultec, https://azultec.de/.\n\n===============================================\n\n[1] G. de Vahl Davis, Natural convection of air in a square cavity: A bench mark numerical solution, Int. J. Numer. Meth. Fluids 3 (3) (1983) 249\u2013264. https://doi.org/10.1002/fld.1650030305.\n\n[2] R. Becker, M. Braack, Solution of a stationary benchmark problem for natural convection with large temperature difference, International Journal of Thermal Sciences 41 (5) (2002) 428\u2013439. https://doi.org/10.1016/S1290-0729(02)01335-2.\n\n[3] J. Vierendeels, B. Merci, E. Dick, Benchmark solutions for the natural convective heat transfer problem in a square cavity with large horizontal temperature differences, Int Jnl of Num Meth for HFF 13 (8) (2003) 1057\u20131078. https://doi.org/10.1108/09615530310501957.\n\n[4] P. Le Qu\u00e9r\u00e9, C. Weisman, H. Paill\u00e8re, J. Vierendeels, E. Dick, R. Becker, M. Braack, J. Locke, Modelling of Natural Convection Flows with Large Temperature Differences: A Benchmark Problem for Low Mach Number Solvers. Part 1. Reference Solutions, ESAIM: M2AN 39 (3) (2005) 609\u2013616. https://doi.org/10.1051/m2an:2005027.\n\n[5] S. Lenz, M. Krafczyk, M. Geier, S. Chen, Z. Guo, Validation of a two-dimensional gas-kinetic scheme for compressible natural convection on structured and unstructured meshes, International Journal of Thermal Sciences 136 (2019) 299\u2013315. https://doi.org/10.1016/j.ijthermalsci.2018.10.004.", "title": "Turbulent natural convection in cavity at large temperature difference"}, "statistics": {"commentCount": "0", "viewCount": "47", "likeCount": "2", "dislikeCount": "0", "favoriteCount": "0"}, "contentDetails": {"duration": "PT29S"}}], "idx_paper": "10.1016/j.gr.2018.10.004"}, {"q": "10.1016/j.gr.2018.10.004", "items": [{"id": "qsdd30cuSHM", "snippet": {"channelTitle": "Stephan Lenz", "channelId": "UCyG_vyKaiFMzdQqf5RhvQmg", "defaultAudioLanguage": "zxx", "publishedAt": "2019-08-29T10:28:21Z", "tags": ["CFD", "GKS", "Gas-Kinetic Scheme", "GPGPU", "Tesla P100", "High Rayleigh number", "Flow Simulation", "CUDA", "TU Braunschweig", "iRMB", "Fire Simulation", "Fire", "Burning Room", "Brandsimulation", "DFG", "GRK2075", "VirtualFluids", "Feuer", "Computational Fluid Dynamics", "Str\u00f6mungssimulation", "Feuer Simulation"], "description": "This video shows a simulation of a fire burning in a room that is ventilated by a single window. The burning obstruction is modeled by a gaseous fuel supply with prescribed heat release rate. The combustion is modeled under the \"mixed is burned\" assumption with the single reaction of methane and oxygen reacting to carbon dioxide and water.\n\nThe simulation was performed with the research CFD code VirtualFluids, developed at the Institute for Computational Modeling in Civil Engineering of the Technische Universit\u00e4t Braunschweig (https://www.tu-braunschweig.de/irmb). More specific, the gas kinetic scheme branch of VirtualFluids, developed by Stephan Lenz, was used. Gas Kinetic Schemes (GKS) [1] provide an alternative approach to the solution of the compressible Navier-Stokes equations by utilizing the gas evolution equation on the mesoscopic scale, i.e. Boltzmann equation, instead of the macroscopic equations, i.e. Navier-Stokes equations.\n\nThe chemistry part of the fire model is inspired by the Fire Dynamics Simulator (FDS), which can be considered as state-of-the-art in fire simulation (see https://pages.nist.gov/fds-smv/).\n\nVirtualFluids GKS utilizes massive parallelization on multiple GPGPUs. The simulation of a minute of flame evolution took about 2 hours on four NVIDIA Tesla P100 GPGPUs. The room and the exterior are discretized by an octree based Cartesian grid with 4 levels of refinement, more than 4 million cells and a resolution of about one centimeter in the plume above the obstruction.\n\nValidation of GKS for thermal compressible flows in two dimensions was published in [2] and [3]. The present simulation was obtained with the three dimensional extension of the code used in [3]. Validation of the three dimensional code for the simulation of fire is work in progress and will be published soon. By now, good agreement to experimental data was obtained for Purdue and Sandia flames (see FDS Validation Guide for details on the benchmarks, https://pages.nist.gov/fds-smv/manuals.html).\n\nParaview was used for visualization. The flame is visualized as volume rendering of the gas temperature. The smoke is a volume rendering of the combustion products mass fraction.\n\nThis work was finanzed by the German Research Foundation (DFG) under the framework of Research Training Group GRK 2075.\n\nRemark: Flame and smoke visualization are tuned for visual appearance.\n\n[1] K. Xu, A Gas-Kinetic BGK Scheme for the Navier\u2013Stokes Equations and Its Connection with Artificial Dissipation and Godunov Method, Journal of Computational Physics 171 (1) (2001) 289\u2013335. https://doi.org/10.1006/jcph.2001.6790.\n\n[2] S. Enzymes.\n\nPyridoxine activates many different enzymes in the plant cell and it contributes to many various physiological processes. It has been examined for stimulating and enhancing banana fruit 'Williams' (Giant Cavendish AAA sub-gathering) during12 days of the shelf life. Many different concentrations of vitamin B6 0, 3, 6, 9, and 12mM have been applied to bananas for 30 min. Thereafter, fruit stored at room temperature (25 \u00b1 1oC and air humidity average 56 \u00b1 2%) for twelve days. Fruit samples were selected each 3-day intervals. The physical and chemical analysis was determined to evaluate fruit ripening quality elements. The physical quality attributes of fruit were measured (brown skin spot index and color hue angle). Additionally, the chemical properties determinations were investigated such as starch content and starch catalyst breakdown activities, for example, a-amylase (AMY; EC: 3.2.1.1), phosphorylase (PHO; EC: 2.4.1.14), and invertase (INV; EC: 3.2.1.26). The sugar profile (reducing, non-reducing, and total sugar content) was estimated. In term of fruit quality parameter, peel fruit firmness, degradation of chlorophyll, and \u00df-carotene content were measured during the shelf life period. Pyridoxine treatment at 9mM gives a higher starch breakdown and total soluble sugars. Moreover, increasing the \u00df-carotene content of fruit peel which reflects on the color hue angle of fruit. While the decreases in both total chlorophyll and phenol content were observed after treating by Vit. B6 during the shelf-life period. Also, fruit presented a normal ripening proprieties and less ripening fruit spotting index under moderate browning symptoms index 12th day. It was concluded that pyridoxine application at 9mM has generative effects on fruit ripening and optimize the quality of \u2018Williams\u2019 banana at room temperature to normal ripening. A conjectured formula for the coefficients in this basis was given earlier in 2019 by Alexandersson. We give a new proof of D\u2019Adderio\u2019s result which also proves the conjectured formula. As a consequence, we also obtain new formulas in the area of diagonal harmonics. The problem of finding e-expansion for vertical-strip LLT polynomials is surprisingly similar to the still open problem of Shareshian\u2013Wachs, regarding the e-expansion of chromatic quasisymmetric polynomials associated with unit-interval graphs.
